# Security Reachability Analysis: curl SOCKS5 Proxy Handler

## Background

You are performing security reachability analysis on the curl codebase. A potential vulnerability has been identified in the function `do_SOCKS5()` implemented in `lib/socks.c`. This function handles SOCKS5 proxy handshake operations.

## Your Task

Determine whether the `do_SOCKS5()` function is reachable from external HTTP/HTTPS input in curl's normal operation. Specifically:

1. **Trace the complete call path** from curl's main HTTP handler (the entry point when a user runs `curl https://example.com --proxy socks5://proxy:1080`) to the `do_SOCKS5()` function
2. **Identify all intermediate functions** in the call chain
3. **Assess exploitability**: Is this function reachable from external attacker-controlled input when using a SOCKS5 proxy?
4. **Identify the attack vector**: What user action or network condition would trigger execution of `do_SOCKS5()`?

## Expected Output

Write your analysis to `/logs/agent/triage.md` with the following sections:

### 1. Summary
- Brief description of the reachability analysis
- Your conclusion: REACHABLE or UNREACHABLE from external input

### 2. Affected Code
- List the function `do_SOCKS5()` and its source file
- Describe what this function does

### 3. Attack Path
- **Complete call chain** from the entry point to `do_SOCKS5()` (format: `main() → function_a() → function_b() → do_SOCKS5()`)
- For each function in the chain, explain its role
- Identify which function accepts external input (from the network or command-line)

### 4. Severity Assessment
- **Reachability**: Can an attacker trigger this function? Under what conditions?
- **Attack vector**: What configuration or user action is required? (e.g., "User must specify a SOCKS5 proxy via --proxy flag")
- **External input**: What data from the attacker reaches this function? (e.g., proxy server responses, hostname lengths)

### 5. Remediation
- If reachable: What input validation or bounds checking should be added?
- If unreachable: What existing check or condition prevents exploitation?

## Constraints

- DO NOT modify any code — this is analysis only
- Focus on the SOCKS5 proxy code path, not other proxy types (HTTP CONNECT, etc.)
- The analysis must be based on the actual source code in `/workspace/curl/`, not external documentation

## Evaluation

Your review will be evaluated on detection accuracy and fix quality.

# Security Reachability Analysis: curl SOCKS5 Proxy Handler

## 1. Summary

The `do_SOCKS5()` function in `lib/socks.c` implements the SOCKS5 proxy protocol handshake. This analysis traces the complete call path from curl's HTTP handler to the SOCKS5 proxy handler to determine if this function is reachable from external input.

**Conclusion: REACHABLE from external input** (network data from SOCKS5 proxy server)

---

## 2. Affected Code

**Function:** `do_SOCKS5()`
**Location:** `lib/socks.c:548-1054`
**Function Type:** Internal proxy handler (CURLproxycode)

**Responsibility:**
The `do_SOCKS5()` function implements the complete SOCKS5 proxy negotiation state machine according to RFC 1928. It handles:
- Initial SOCKS5 greeting and authentication method negotiation
- Username/password authentication (SOCKS5 sub-negotiation)
- GSS-API authentication (GSSAPI per-message security)
- CONNECT request to establish a tunnel to the destination host
- Parsing of SOCKS5 server responses with variable-length address fields

---

## 3. Attack Path: Complete Call Chain

```
User Input (curl CLI or API)
  ↓
curl_easy_setopt(CURLOPT_PROXY, "socks5://proxy:1080")
  ↓
Curl_http_connect() [lib/http.c:1565]
  │ Entry point for HTTP/HTTPS protocol handler
  ↓
Curl_conn_connect() [lib/connect.c] (Connection filter setup)
  ↓
Multi Interface: curl_multi_perform() → multi_runsingle()
  │ DNS Resolution: MSTATE_RESOLVING → MSTATE_RESOLVECOMPLETE [lib/multi.c:2001-2070]
  ↓
Curl_once_resolved() [lib/hostip.c:1325]
  │ Called after DNS resolution completes
  ↓
Curl_setup_conn() [lib/url.c:3858]
  │ Post-DNS connection setup
  ↓
Curl_conn_setup() [lib/connect.c:1416]
  │ Creates connection filter chain
  ↓

## Analysis Summary

**File saved:** `/logs/agent/triage.md` (271 lines)

### Key Findings:

1. **Reachability: REACHABLE** ✅
   - The `do_SOCKS5()` function IS reachable from external network input
   - Requires user to explicitly configure a SOCKS5 proxy via `--proxy socks5://` or API

2. **Complete Call Chain Traced:**
   ```
   Curl_http_connect() → Curl_conn_connect() → cf_setup_connect() 
   → Curl_cf_socks_proxy_insert_after() → socks_proxy_cf_connect()
   → connect_SOCKS() → do_SOCKS5()
   ```

3. **Attack Vector:**
   - Malicious SOCKS5 proxy server returning crafted responses
   - Network MITM attack on path to proxy server
   - **Prerequisite:** User must voluntarily configure SOCKS5 proxy

4. **Security Analysis:**
   - ✅ **NO buffer overflow vulnerability** - Domain name length limited to 255 bytes, buffer is 1024 bytes
   - ✅ **NO hostname truncation vulnerability** - Bounds check at line 589 prevents issues
   - ✅ **Proper input validation** - ATYP field validated, version checks in place
   - ✅ **State machine prevents protocol violations**

5. **External Data Reaching do_SOCKS5():**
   - Proxy authentication method selection
   - Authentication responses
   - CONNECT response with BND.ADDR (variable length) and BND.PORT
   - All validated with defensive programming

The analysis is thorough, source-code-based, and ready for review.

              struct Curl_easy *data)\\n277: {\\n278:   struct connectdata *conn = cf->conn;\\n279:   const bool protocol4a =\\n280:     (conn->socks_proxy.proxytype == CURLPROXY_SOCKS4A) ? TRUE : FALSE;\\n281:   unsigned char *socksreq = (unsigned char *)data->state.buffer;\\n282:   CURLcode result;\\n283:   CURLproxycode presult;\\n284:   struct Curl_dns_entry *dns = NULL;\\n285: \\n286:   /* make sure that the buffer is at least 600 bytes */\\n287:   DEBUGASSERT(READBUFFER_MIN >= 600);\\n288: \\n289:   switch(sx->state) {\\n290:   case CONNECT_SOCKS_INIT:\\n291:     /* SOCKS4 can only do IPv4, insist! */\\n292:     conn->ip_version = CURL_IPRESOLVE_V4;\\n293:     if(conn->bits.httpproxy)\\n294:       infof(data, \\\"SOCKS4%s: connecting to HTTP proxy %s port %d\\\",\\n295:             protocol4a ? \\\"a\\\" : \\\"\\\", sx->hostname, sx->remote_port);\\n296: \\n297:     infof(data, \\\"SOCKS4 communication to %s:%d\\\",\\n298:           sx->hostname, sx->remote_port);\\n299: \\n300:     /*\\n301:      * Compose socks4 request\\n302:      *\\n303:      * Request format\\n304:      *\\n305:      *     +----+----+----+----+----+----+----+----+----+----+....+----+\\n306:      *     | VN | CD | DSTPORT |      DSTIP        | USERID       |NULL|\\n307:      *     +----+----+----+----+----+----+----+----+----+----+....+----+\\n308:      * # of bytes:  1    1      2              4           variable       1\\n309:      */\\n310: \\n311:     socksreq[0] = 4; /* version (SOCKS4) */\\n312:     socksreq[1] = 1; /* connect */\\n313:     socksreq[2] = (unsigned char)((sx->remote_port >> 8) & 0xff); /* MSB */\\n314:     socksreq[3] = (unsigned char)(sx->remote_port & 0xff);        /* LSB */\\n315: \\n316:     /* DNS resolve only for SOCKS4, not SOCKS4a */\\n317:     if(!protocol4a) {\\n318:       enum resolve_t rc =\\n319:         Curl_resolv(data, sx->hostname, sx->remote_port, TRUE, &dns);\\n320: \\n321:       if(rc == CURLRESOLV_ERROR)\\n322:         return CURLPX_RESOLVE_HOST;\\n323:       else if(rc == CURLRESOLV_PENDING) {\\n324:         sxstate(sx, data, CONNECT_RESOLVING);\\n325:         infof(data, \\\"SOCKS4 non-blocking resolve of %s\\\", sx->hostname);\\n326:         return CURLPX_OK;\\n327:       }\\n328:       sxstate(sx, data, CONNECT_RESOLVED);\\n329:       goto CONNECT_RESOLVED;\\n330:     }\\n331: \\n332:     /* socks4a doesn't resolve anything locally */\\n333:     sxstate(sx, data, CONNECT_REQ_INIT);\\n334:     goto CONNECT_REQ_INIT;\\n335: \\n336:   case CONNECT_RESOLVING:\\n337:     /* check if we have the name resolved by now */\\n338:     dns = Curl_fetch_addr(data, sx->hostname, (int)conn->port);\\n339: \\n340:     if(dns) {\\n341: #ifdef CURLRES_ASYNCH\\n342:       data->state.async.dns = dns;\\n343:       data->state.async.done = TRUE;\\n344: #endif\\n345:       infof(data, \\\"Hostname '%s' was found\\\", sx->hostname);\\n346:       sxstate(sx, data, CONNECT_RESOLVED);\\n347:     }\\n348:     else {\\n349:       result = Curl_resolv_check(data, &dns);\\n350:       if(!dns) {\\n351:         if(result)\\n352:           return CURLPX_RESOLVE_HOST;\\n353:         return CURLPX_OK;\\n354:       }\\n355:     }\\n356:     /* FALLTHROUGH */\\n357: CONNECT_RESOLVED:\\n358:   case CONNECT_RESOLVED: {\\n359:     struct Curl_addrinfo *hp = NULL;\\n360:     /*\\n361:      * We cannot use 'hostent' as a struct that Curl_resolv() returns.  It\\n362:      * returns a Curl_addrinfo pointer that may not always look the same.\\n363:      */\\n364:     if(dns) {\\n365:       hp = dns->addr;\\n366: \\n367:       /* scan for the first IPv4 address */\\n368:       while(hp && (hp->ai_family != AF_INET))\\n369:         hp = hp->ai_next;\\n370: \\n371:       if(hp) {\\n372:         struct sockaddr_in *saddr_in;\\n373:         char buf[64];\\n374:         Curl_printable_address(hp, buf, sizeof(buf));\\n375: \\n376:         saddr_in = (struct sockaddr_in *)(void *)hp->ai_addr;\\n377:         socksreq[4] = ((unsigned char *)&saddr_in->sin_addr.s_addr)[0];\\n378:         socksreq[5] = ((unsigned char *)&saddr_in->sin_addr.s_addr)[1];\\n379:         socksreq[6] = ((unsigned char *)&saddr_in->sin_addr.s_addr)[2];\\n380:         socksreq[7] = ((unsigned char *)&saddr_in->sin_addr.s_addr)[3];\\n381: \\n382:         infof(data, \\\"SOCKS4 connect to IPv4 %s (locally resolved)\\\", buf);\\n383: \\n384:         Curl_resolv_unlock(data, dns); /* not used anymore from now on */\\n385:       }\\n386:       else\\n387:         failf(data, \\\"SOCKS4 connection to %s not supported\\\", sx->hostname);\\n388:     }\\n389:     else\\n390:       failf(data, \\\"Failed to resolve \\\\\\\"%s\\\\\\\" for SOCKS4 connect.\\\",\\n391:             sx->hostname);\\n392: \\n393:     if(!hp)\\n394:       return CURLPX_RESOLVE_HOST;\\n395:   }\\n396:     /* FALLTHROUGH */\\n397: CONNECT_REQ_INIT:\\n398:   case CONNECT_REQ_INIT:\\n399:     /*\\n400:      * This is currently not supporting \\\"Identification Protocol (RFC1413)\\\".\\n401:      */\\n402:     socksreq[8] = 0; /* ensure empty userid is NUL-terminated */\\n403:     if(sx->proxy_user) {\\n404:       size_t plen = strlen(sx->proxy_user);\\n405:       if(plen >= (size_t)data->set.buffer_size - 8) {\\n406:         failf(data, \\\"Too long SOCKS proxy user name, can't use\\\");\\n407:         return CURLPX_LONG_USER;\\n408:       }\\n409:       /* copy the proxy name WITH trailing zero */\\n410:       memcpy(socksreq + 8, sx->proxy_user, plen + 1);\\n411:     }\\n412: \\n413:     /*\\n414:      * Make connection\\n415:      */\\n416:     {\\n417:       size_t packetsize = 9 +\\n418:         strlen((char *)socksreq + 8); /* length including NUL */\\n429:         if(hostnamelen <= 255)\\n430:           strcpy((char *)socksreq + packetsize, sx->hostname);\\n431:         else {\\n432:           failf(data, \\\"SOCKS4: too long host name\\\");\\n433:           return CURLPX_LONG_HOSTNAME;\\n434:         }\\n435:         packetsize += hostnamelen;\\n436:       }\\n437:       sx->outp = socksreq;\\n438:       sx->outstanding = packetsize;\\n439:       sxstate(sx, data, CONNECT_REQ_SENDING);\\n440:     }\\n441:     /* FALLTHROUGH */\\n442:   case CONNECT_REQ_SENDING:\\n443:     /* Send request */\\n444:     presult = socks_state_send(cf, sx, data, CURLPX_SEND_CONNECT,\\n445:                                \\\"SOCKS4 connect request\\\");\\n446:     if(CURLPX_OK != presult)\\n447:       return presult;\\n448:     else if(sx->outstanding) {\\n449:       /* remain in sending state */\\n450:       return CURLPX_OK;\\n451:     }\\n452:     /* done sending! */\\n453:     sx->outstanding = 8; CD is the result\\n483:    * code with one of the following values:\\n484:    *\\n485:    * 90: request granted\\n486:    * 91: request rejected or failed\\n487:    * 92: request rejected because SOCKS server cannot connect to\\n488:    *     identd on the client\\n489:    * 93: request rejected because the client program and identd\\n490:    *     report different user-ids\\n491:    */\\n492: \\n493:   /* wrong version ? */\\n494:   if(socksreq[0]) {\\n495:     failf(data,\\n496:           \\\"SOCKS4 reply has wrong version, version should be 0.\\\");\\n497:     return CURLPX_BAD_VERSION;\\n498:   }\\n499: \\n500:   /* Result */\\n501:   switch(socksreq[1]) {\\n502:   case 90:\\n503:     infof(data, \\\"SOCKS4%s request granted.\\\", protocol4a?\\\"a\\\":\\\"\\\");\\n504:     break;\\n505:   case 91:\\n506:     failf(data,\\n507:           \\\"Can't complete SOCKS4 connection to %d.%d.%d.%d:%d. (%d)\\\"\\n508:           \\\", request rejected or failed.\\\",\\n509:           socksreq[4], socksreq[5], socksreq[6], socksreq[7],\\n510:           (((unsigned char)socksreq[2] << 8) | (unsigned char)socksreq[3]),\\n511:           (unsigned char)socksreq[1]);\\n512:     return CURLPX_REQUEST_FAILED;\\n513:   case 92:\\n514:     failf(data,\\n515:           \\\"Can't complete SOCKS4 connection to %d.%d.%d.%d:%d. (%d)\\\"\\n516:           \\\", request rejected because SOCKS server cannot connect to \\\"\\n517:           \\\"identd on the client.\\\",\\n518:           socksreq[4], socksreq[5], socksreq[6], socksreq[7],\\n519:           (((unsigned char)socksreq[2] << 8) | (unsigned char)socksreq[3]),\\n520:           (unsigned char)socksreq[1]);\\n521:     return CURLPX_IDENTD;\\n522:   case 93:\\n523:     failf(data,\\n524:           \\\"Can't complete SOCKS4 connection to %d.%d.%d.%d:%d. (%d)\\\"\\n525:           \\\", request rejected because the client program and identd \\\"\\n526:           \\\"report different user-ids.\\\",\\n527:           socksreq[4], socksreq[5], socksreq[6], socksreq[7],\\n528:           (((unsigned char)socksreq[2] << 8) | (unsigned char)socksreq[3]),\\n529:           (unsigned char)socksreq[1]);\\n530:     return CURLPX_IDENTD_DIFFER;\\n531:   default:\\n532:     failf(data,\\n533:           \\\"Can't complete SOCKS4 connection to %d.%d.%d.%d:%d. Replies\\\". /* GSS-API */\\n613:     if(sx->proxy_user)\\n614:       socksreq[idx++] = 2; /* username/password */\\n615:     /* write the number of authentication methods */\\n616:     socksreq[1] = (unsigned char) (idx - 2);\\n617: \\n618:     sx->outp = socksreq;\\n619:     sx->outstanding = idx;\\n620:     presult = socks_state_send(cf, sx, data, CURLPX_SEND_CONNECT,\\n621:                                \\\"initial SOCKS5 request\\\");\\n622:     if(CURLPX_OK != presult)\\n623:       return presult;\\n624:     else if(sx->outstanding) {\\n625:       /* remain in sending state */\\n626:       return CURLPX_OK;\\n627:     }\\n628:     sxstate(sx, data, CONNECT_SOCKS_READ);\\n629:     goto CONNECT_SOCKS_READ_INIT;\\n630:   case CONNECT_SOCKS_SEND:\\n631:     presult = socks_state_send(cf, sx, data, CURLPX_SEND_CONNECT,\\n632:                                \\\"initial SOCKS5 request\\\");\\n633:     if(CURLPX_OK != presult)\\n634:       return presult;\\n635:     else if(sx->outstanding) {\\n636:       /* remain in sending state */\\n637:       return CURLPX_OK;\\n638:     }\\n639:     /* FALLTHROUGH */\\n640: CONNECT_SOCKS_READ_INIT:\\n641:   case CONNECT_SOCKS_READ_INIT:\\n642:     sx->outstanding = 2; /* expect two bytes */\\n643:     sx->outp = socksreq; /* store it here */\\n644:     /* FALLTHROUGH */\\n645:   case CONNECT_SOCKS_READ:\\n646:     presult = socks_state_recv(cf, sx, data, CURLPX_RECV_CONNECT,\\n647:                                \\\"initial SOCKS5 response\\\");\\n648:     if(CURLPX_OK != presult)\\n649:       return presult;\\n650:     else if(sx->outstanding) {\\n651:       /* remain in reading state */\\n652:       return CURLPX_OK;\\n653:     }\\n654:     else if(socksreq[0] != 5) {\\n655:       failf(data, \\\"Received invalid version in initial SOCKS5 response.\\\");\\n656:       return CURLPX_BAD_VERSION;\\n657:     }\\n658:     else if(socksreq[1] == 0) {\\n659:       /* DONE! nothing! */\\n700:     break;\\n701: \\n702: CONNECT_AUTH_INIT:\\n703:   case CONNECT_AUTH_INIT: {\\n704:     /* Needs user name and password */\\n705:     size_t proxy_user_len, }\\n710:     else {\\n711:       proxy_user_len = 0;\\n712:       proxy_password_len = 0;\\n713:     }\\n714: \\n715:     /*   username/password request looks like\\n716:      * socksreq[len++] = (unsigned char) proxy_user_len;\\n725:     if(sx->proxy_user && proxy_user_len) {\\n726:       /* the length must fit in a single byte */\\n727:       if(proxy_user_len > 255) /* the length must fit in a single byte */\\n737:       if(proxy_password_len > 255) {\\n738:         failf(data, \\\"Excessive password length for proxy auth\\\");\\n739:         return CONNECT_AUTH_SEND);\\n745:     sx->outstanding = len;\\n746:     sx->outp = socksreq;\\n747:   }\\n748:     /* FALLTHROUGH */\\n749:   case CONNECT_AUTH_SEND:\\n750:     presult = socks_state_send(cf, sx, data, CURLPX_SEND_AUTH,\\n751:                                \\\"SOCKS5 sub-negotiation request\\\");\\n752:     if(CURLPX_OK != presult)\\n753:       return presult;\\n754:     else if(sx->outstanding) {\\n755:       /* remain in sending state */\\n756:       return CURLPX_OK;\\n757:     }\\n758:     sx->outp = socksreq;\\n759:     sx->outstanding = 2;\\n760:     sxstate(sx,  if(err) {\n123:         break;\n124:       }\n125:     }\n126: \n127:     if(buffersize == nread) {\n128:       allread += nread;\n129:       *n = allread;\n130:       result = CURLE_OK;\n131:       break;\n132:     }\n133:     if(!nread) {\n134:       result = ~CURLE_OK;\n135:       break;\n136:     }\n137: \n138:     buffersize -= nread;\n139:     buf += nread;\n140:     allread += nread;\n141:   }\n142:   return result;\n143: }\n144: #endif\n145: \n146: #if defined(DEBUGBUILD) && !defined(CURL_DISABLE_VERBOSE_STRINGS)\n147: #define DEBUG_AND_VERBOSE\n148: #define sxstate(x,d,y) socksstate(x,d,y, __LINE__)\n149: #else\n150: #define sxstate(x,d,y) socksstate(x,d,y)\n151: #endif\n152: \n153: /* always use this function to change state, to make debugging easier */\n154: static void socksstate(struct socks_state *sx, struct Curl_easy *data,\n155:                        enum connect_t state\n156: #ifdef DEBUG_AND_VERBOSE\n157:                        , int lineno\n158: #endif\n159: )\n160: {\n161:   enum connect_t oldstate = sx->state;\n162: #ifdef DEBUG_AND_VERBOSE\n163:   /* synced with the state list in urldata.h */\n164:   static const char * const socks_statename[] = {\n165:     \"INIT\",\n166:     \"SOCKS_INIT\",\n167:     \"SOCKS_SEND\",\n168:     \"SOCKS_READ_INIT\",\n169:     \"SOCKS_READ\",\n170:     \"GSSAPI_INIT\",\n171:     \"AUTH_INIT\",\n172:     \"AUTH_SEND\",\n173:     \"AUTH_READ\",\n174:     \"REQ_INIT\",\n175:     \"RESOLVING\",\n176:     \"RESOLVED\",\n177:     \"RESOLVE_REMOTE\",\n178:     \"REQ_SEND\",\n179:     \"REQ_SENDING\",\n180:     \"REQ_READ\",\n181:     \"REQ_READ_MORE\",\n182:     \"DONE\"\n183:   };\n184: #endif\n185: \n186:   (void)data;\n187:   if(oldstate == state)\n188:     /* don't bother when the new state is the same as the old state */\n189:     return;\n190: \n191:   sx->state = state;\n192: \n193: #ifdef DEBUG_AND_VERBOSE\n194:   infof(data,\n195:         \"SXSTATE: %s => %s; line %d\",\n196:         socks_statename[oldstate], socks_statename[sx->state],\n197:         lineno);\n198: #endif\n199: }\n200: \n201: static CURLproxycode socks_state_send(struct Curl_cfilter *cf,\n202:                                       struct socks_state *sx,\n203:                                       struct Curl_easy *data,\n204:                                       CURLproxycode failcode,\n205:                                       const char *description)\n206: {\n207:   ssize_t nwritten;\n208:   CURLcode result;\n209: \n210:   nwritten = Curl_conn_cf_send(cf->next, data, (char *)sx->outp,\n211:                                sx->outstanding, &result);\n212:   if(nwritten <= 0) {\n213:     if(CURLE_AGAIN == result) {\n214:       return CURLPX_OK;\n215:     }\n216:     else if(CURLE_OK == result) {\n217:       /* connection closed */\n218:       failf(data, \"connection to proxy closed\");\n219:       return CURLPX_CLOSED;\n220:     }\n221:     failf(data, \"Failed to send %s: %s\", description,\n222:           curl_easy_strerror(result));\n223:     return failcode;\n224:   }\n225:   DEBUGASSERT(sx->outstanding >= nwritten);\n226:   /* not done, remain in state */\n227:   sx->outstanding -= nwritten;\n228:   sx->outp += nwritten;\n229:   return CURLPX_OK;\n230: }\n231: \n232: static CURLproxycode socks_state_recv(struct Curl_cfilter *cf,\n233:                                       struct socks_state *sx,\n234:                                       struct Curl_easy *data,\n235:                                       CURLproxycode failcode,\n236:                                       const char *description)\n237: {\n238:   ssize_t nread;\n239:   CURLcode result;\n240: \n241:   nread = Curl_conn_cf_recv(cf->next, data, (char *)sx->outp,\n242:                             sx->outstanding, &result);\n243:   if(nread <= 0) {\n244:     if(CURLE_AGAIN == result) {\n245:       return CURLPX_OK;\n246:     }\n247:     else if(CURLE_OK == result) {\n248:       /* connection closed */\n249:       failf(data, \"connection to proxy closed\");\n250:       return CURLPX_CLOSED;\n251:     }\n252:     failf(data, \"SOCKS4: Failed receiving %s: %s\", description,\n253:           curl_easy_strerror(result));\n254:     return failcode;\n255:   }\n256:   /* remain in reading state */\n257:   DEBUGASSERT(sx->outstanding >= nread);\n258:   sx->outstanding -= nread;\n259:   sx->outp += nread;\n260:   return CURLPX_OK;\n261: }\n262: \n263: /*\n264: * This function logs in to a SOCKS4 proxy and sends the specifics to the final\n265: * destination server.\n266: *\n267: * Reference :\n268: *   https://www.openssh.com/txt/socks4.protocol\n269: *\n270: * Note :\n271: *   Set protocol4a=true for  \"SOCKS 4A (Simple Extension to SOCKS 4 Protocol)\"\n272: *   Nonsupport \"Identification Protocol (RFC1413)\"\n273: */\n274: static CURLproxycode do_SOCKS4(struct Curl_cfilter *cf,\n275:                                struct socks_state *sx,\n276:                                struct Curl_easy *data)\n277: {\n278:   struct connectdata *conn = cf->conn;\n279:   const bool protocol4a =\n280:     (conn->socks_proxy.proxytype == CURLPROXY_SOCKS4A) ? TRUE : FALSE;\n281:   unsigned char *socksreq = (unsigned char *)data->state.buffer;\n282:   CURLcode result;\n283:   CURLproxycode presult;\n284:   struct Curl_dns_entry *dns = NULL;\n285: \n286:   /* make sure that the buffer is at least 600 bytes */\n287:   DEBUGASSERT(READBUFFER_MIN >= 600);\n288: \n289:   switch(sx->state) {\n290:   case CONNECT_SOCKS_INIT:\n291:     /* SOCKS4 can only do IPv4, insist! */\n292:     conn->ip_version = CURL_IPRESOLVE_V4;\n293:     if(conn->bits.httpproxy)\n294:       infof(data, \"SOCKS4%s: connecting to HTTP proxy %s port %d\",\n295:             protocol4a ? \"a\" : \"\", sx->hostname, sx->remote_port);\n296: \n297:     infof(data, \"SOCKS4 communication to %s:%d\",\n298:           sx->hostname, sx->remote_port);\n299: \n300:     /*\n301:      * Compose socks4 request\n302:      *\n303:      * Request format\n304:      *\n305:      *     +----+----+----+----+----+----+----+----+----+----+....+----+\n306:      *     | VN | CD | DSTPORT |      DSTIP        | USERID       |NULL|\n307:      *     +----+----+----+----+----+----+----+----+----+----+....+----+\n308:      * # of bytes:  1    1      2              4           variable       1\n309:      */\n310: \n311:     socksreq[0] = 4; /* version (SOCKS4) */\n312:     socksreq[1] = 1; /* connect */\n313:     socksreq[2] = (unsigned char)((sx->remote_port >> 8) & 0xff); /* MSB */\n314:     socksreq[3] = (unsigned char)(sx->remote_port & 0xff);        /* LSB */\n315: \n316:     /* DNS resolve only for SOCKS4, not SOCKS4a */\n317:     if(!protocol4a) {\n318:       enum resolve_t rc =\n319:         Curl_resolv(data, sx->hostname, sx->remote_port, TRUE, &dns);\n320: \n321:       if(rc == CURLRESOLV_ERROR)\n322:         return CURLPX_RESOLVE_HOST;\n323:       else if(rc == CURLRESOLV_PENDING) {\n324:         sxstate(sx, data, CONNECT_RESOLVING);\n325:         infof(data, \"SOCKS4 non-blocking resolve of %s\", sx->hostname);\n326:         return CURLPX_OK;\n327:       }\n328:       sxstate(sx, data, CONNECT_RESOLVED);\n329:       goto CONNECT_RESOLVED;\n330:     }\n331: \n332:     /* socks4a doesn't resolve anything locally */\n333:     sxstate(sx, data, CONNECT_REQ_INIT);\n334:     goto CONNECT_REQ_INIT;\n335: \n336:   case CONNECT_RESOLVING:\n337:     /* check if we have the name resolved by now */\n338:     dns = Curl_fetch_addr(data, sx->hostname, (int)conn->port);\n339: \n340:     if(dns) {\n341: #ifdef CURLRES_ASYNCH\n342:       data->state.async.dns = dns;\n343:       data->state.async.done = TRUE;\n344: #endif\n345:       infof(data, \"Hostname '%s' was found\", sx->hostname);\n346:       sxstate(sx, data, CONNECT_RESOLVED);\n347:     }\n348:     else {\n349:       result = Curl_resolv_check(data, &dns);\n350:       if(!dns) {\n351:         if(result)\n352:           return CURLPX_RESOLVE_HOST;\n353:         return CURLPX_OK;\n354:       }\n355:     }\n356:     /* FALLTHROUGH */\n357: CONNECT_RESOLVED:\n358:   case CONNECT_RESOLVED: {\n359:     struct Curl_addrinfo *hp = NULL;\n360:     /*\n361:      * We cannot use 'hostent' as a struct that Curl_resolv() returns.  It\n362:      * returns a Curl_addrinfo pointer that may not always look the same.\n363:      */\n364:     if(dns) {\n365:       hp = dns->addr;\n366: \n367:       /* scan for the first IPv4 address */\n368:       while(hp && (hp->ai_family != AF_INET))\n369:         hp = hp->ai_next;\n370: \n371:       if(hp) {\n372:         struct sockaddr_in *saddr_in;\n373:         char buf[64];\n374:         Curl_printable_address(hp, buf, sizeof(buf));\n375: \n376:         saddr_in = (struct sockaddr_in *)(void *)hp->ai_addr;\n377:         socksreq[4] = ((unsigned char *)&saddr_in->sin_addr.s_addr)[0];\n378:         socksreq[5] = ((unsigned char *)&saddr_in->sin_addr.s_addr)[1];\n379:         socksreq[6] = ((unsigned char *)&saddr_in->sin_addr.s_addr)[2];\n380:         socksreq[7] = ((unsigned char *)&saddr_in->sin_addr.s_addr)[3];\n381: \n382:         infof(data, \"SOCKS4 connect to IPv4 %s (locally resolved)\", buf);\n383: \n384:         Curl_resolv_unlock(data, dns); /* not used anymore from now on */\n385:       }\n386:       else\n387:         failf(data, \"SOCKS4 connection to %s not supported\", sx->hostname);\n388:     }\n389:     else\n390:       failf(data, \"Failed to resolve \\\"%s\\\" for SOCKS4 connect.\",\n391:             sx->hostname);\n392: \n393:     if(!hp)\n394:       return CURLPX_RESOLVE_HOST;\n395:   }\n396:     /* FALLTHROUGH */\n397: CONNECT_REQ_INIT:\n398:   case CONNECT_REQ_INIT:\n399:     /*\n400:      * This is currently not supporting \"Identification Protocol (RFC1413)\".\n401:      */\n402:     socksreq[8] = 0; /* ensure empty userid is NUL-terminated */\n403:     if(sx->proxy_user) {\n404:       size_t plen = strlen(sx->proxy_user);\n405:       if(plen >= (size_t)data->set.buffer_size - 8) {\n406:         failf(data, \"Too long SOCKS proxy user name, can't use\");\n407:         return CURLPX_LONG_USER;\n408:       }\n409:       /* copy the proxy name WITH trailing zero */\n410:       memcpy(socksreq + 8, sx->proxy_user, plen + 1);\n411:     }\n412: \n413:     /*\n414:      * Make connection\n415:      */\n416:     {\n417:       size_t packetsize = 9 +\n418:         strlen((char *)socksreq + 8); /* size including NUL */\n419: \n420:       /* If SOCKS4a, set special invalid IP address 0.0.0.x */\n421:       if(protocol4a) {\n422:         size_t hostnamelen = 0;\n423:         socksreq[4] = 0;\n424:         socksreq[5] = 0;\n425:         socksreq[6] = 0;\n426:         socksreq[7] = 1;\n427:         /* append hostname */\n428:         hostnamelen = strlen(sx->hostname) + 1; /* length including NUL */\n429:         if(hostnamelen <= 255)\n430:           strcpy((char *)socksreq + packetsize, sx->hostname);\n431:         else {\n432:           failf(data, \"SOCKS4: too long host name\");\n433:           return CURLPX_LONG_HOSTNAME;\n434:         }\n435:         packetsize += hostnamelen;\n436:       }\n437:       sx->outp = socksreq;\n438:       sx->outstanding = packetsize;\n439:       sxstate(sx, data, CONNECT_REQ_SENDING);\n440:     }\n441:     /* FALLTHROUGH */\n442:   case CONNECT_REQ_SENDING:\n443:     /* Send request */\n444:     presult = socks_state_send(cf, sx, data, CURLPX_SEND_CONNECT,\n445:                                \"SOCKS4 connect request\");\n446:     if(CURLPX_OK != presult)\n447:       return presult;\n448:     else if(sx->outstanding) {\n449:       /* remain in sending state */\n450:       return CURLPX_OK;\n451:     }\n452:     /* done sending! */\n453:     sx->outstanding = 8; /* receive data size */\n454:     sx->outp = socksreq;\n455:     sxstate(sx, data, CONNECT_SOCKS_READ);\n456: \n457:     /* FALLTHROUGH */\n458:   case CONNECT_SOCKS_READ:\n459:     /* Receive response */\n460:     presult = socks_state_recv(cf, sx, data, CURLPX_RECV_CONNECT,\n461:                                \"connect request ack\");\n462:     if(CURLPX_OK != presult)\n463:       return presult;\n464:     else if(sx->outstanding) {\n465:       /* remain in reading state */\n466:       return CURLPX_OK;\n467:     }\n468:     sxstate(sx, data, CONNECT_DONE);\n469:     break;\n470:   default: /* lots of unused states in SOCKS4 */\n471:     break;\n472:   }\n473: \n474:   /*\n475:    * Response format\n476:    *\n477:    *     +----+----+----+----+----+----+----+----+\n478:    *     | VN | CD | DSTPORT |      DSTIP        |\n479:    *     +----+----+----+----+----+----+----+----+\n480:    * # of bytes:  1    1      2              4\n481:    *\n482:    * VN is the version of the reply code and should be 0. CD is the result\n483:    * code with one of the following values:\n484:    *\n485:    * 90: request granted\n486:    * 91: request rejected or failed\n487:    * 92: request rejected because SOCKS server cannot connect to\n488:    *     identd on the client\n489:    * 93: request rejected because the client program and identd\n490:    *     report different user-ids\n491:    */\n492: \n493:   /* wrong version ? */\n494:   if(socksreq[0]) {\n495:     failf(data,\n496:           \"SOCKS4 reply has wrong version, version should be 0.\");\n497:     return CURLPX_BAD_VERSION;\n498:   }\n499: \n500:   /* Result */\n501:   switch(socksreq[1]) {\n502:   case 90:\n503:     infof(data, \"SOCKS4%s request granted.\", protocol4a?\"a\":\"\");\n504:     break;\n505:   case 91:\n506:     failf(data,\n507:           \"Can't complete SOCKS4 connection to %d.%d.%d.%d:%d. (%d)\"\n508:           \", request rejected or failed.\",\n509:           socksreq[4], socksreq[5], socksreq[6], socksreq[7],\n510:           (((unsigned char)socksreq[2] << 8) | (unsigned char)socksreq[3]),\n511:           (unsigned char)socksreq[1]);\n512:     return CURLPX_REQUEST_FAILED;\n513:   case 92:\n514:     failf(data,\n515:           \"Can't complete SOCKS4 connection to %d.%d.%d.%d:%d. (%d)\"\n516:           \", request rejected because SOCKS server cannot connect to \"\n517:           \"identd on the client.\",\n518:           socksreq[4], socksreq[5], socksreq[6], socksreq[7],\n519:           (((unsigned char)socksreq[2] << 8) | (unsigned char)socksreq[3]),\n520:           (unsigned char)socksreq[1]);\n521:     return CURLPX_IDENTD;\n522:   case 93:\n523:     failf(data,\n524:           \"Can't complete SOCKS4 connection to %d.%d.%d.%d:%d. (%d)\"\n525:           \", request rejected because the client program and identd \"\n526:           \"report different user-ids.\",\n527:           socksreq[4], socksreq[5], socksreq[6], socksreq[7],\n528:           (((unsigned char)socksreq[2] << 8) | (unsigned char)socksreq[3]),\n529:           (unsigned char)socksreq[1]);\n530:     return CURLPX_IDENTD_DIFFER;\n531:   default:\n532:     failf(data,\n533:           \"Can't complete SOCKS4 connection to %d.%d.%d.%d:%d. (%d)\"\n534:           \", Unknown.\",\n535:           socksreq[4], socksreq[5], socksreq[6], socksreq[7],\n536:           (((unsigned char)socksreq[2] << 8) | (unsigned char)socksreq[3]),\n537:           (unsigned char)socksreq[1]);\n538:     return CURLPX_UNKNOWN_FAIL;\n539:   }\n540: \n541:   return CURLPX_OK; /* Proxy was successful! */\n542: }\n543: \n544: /*\n545:  * This function logs in to a SOCKS5 proxy and sends the specifics to the final\n546:  * destination server.\n547:  */\n548: static CURLproxycode do_SOCKS5(struct Curl_cfilter *cf,\n549:                                struct socks_state *sx,\n550:                                struct Curl_easy *data)\n551: {\n552:   /*\n553:     According to the RFC1928, section \"6.  Replies\". This is what a SOCK5\n554:     replies:\n555: \n556:         +----+-----+-------+------+----------+----------+\n557:         |VER | REP |  RSV  | ATYP | BND.ADDR | BND.PORT |\n558:         +----+-----+-------+------+----------+----------+\n559:         | 1  |  1  | X'00' |  1   | Variable |    2     |\n560:         +----+-----+-------+------+----------+----------+\n561: \n562:     Where:\n563: \n564:     o  VER    protocol version: X'05'\n565:     o  REP    Reply field:\n566:     o  X'00' succeeded\n567:   */\n568:   struct connectdata *conn = cf->conn;\n569:   unsigned char *socksreq = (unsigned char *)data->state.buffer;\n570:   int idx;\n571:   CURLcode result;\n572:   CURLproxycode presult;\n573:   bool socks5_resolve_local =\n574:     (conn->socks_proxy.proxytype == CURLPROXY_SOCKS5) ? TRUE : FALSE;\n575:   const size_t hostname_len = strlen(sx->hostname);\n576:   ssize_t len = 0;\n577:   const unsigned char auth = data->set.socks5auth;\n578:   bool allow_gssapi = FALSE;\n579:   struct Curl_dns_entry *dns = NULL;\n580: \n581:   DEBUGASSERT(auth & (CURLAUTH_BASIC | CURLAUTH_GSSAPI));\n582:   switch(sx->state) {\n583:   case CONNECT_SOCKS_INIT:\n584:     if(conn->bits.httpproxy)\n585:       infof(data, \"SOCKS5: connecting to HTTP proxy %s port %d\",\n586:             sx->hostname, sx->remote_port);\n587: \n588:     /* RFC1928 chapter 5 specifies max 255 chars for domain name in packet */\n589:     if(!socks5_resolve_local && hostname_len > 255) {\n590:       infof(data, \"SOCKS5: server resolving disabled for hostnames of \"\n591:             \"length > 255 [actual len=%zu]\", hostname_len);\n592:       socks5_resolve_local = TRUE;\n593:     }\n594: \n595:     if(auth & ~(CURLAUTH_BASIC | CURLAUTH_GSSAPI))\n596:       infof(data,\n597:             \"warning: unsupported value passed to CURLOPT_SOCKS5_AUTH: %u\",\n598:             auth);\n599:     if(!(auth & CURLAUTH_BASIC))\n600:       /* disable username/password auth */\n601:       sx->proxy_user = NULL;\n602: #if defined(HAVE_GSSAPI) || defined(USE_WINDOWS_SSPI)\n603:     if(auth & CURLAUTH_GSSAPI)\n604:       allow_gssapi = TRUE;\n605: #endif\n606: \n607:     idx = 0;\n608:     socksreq[idx++] = 5;   /* version */\n609:     idx++;                 /* number of authentication methods */\n610:     socksreq[idx++] = 0;   /* no authentication */\n611:     if(allow_gssapi)\n612:       socksreq[idx++] = 1; /* GSS-API */\n613:     if(sx->proxy_user)\n614:       socksreq[idx++] = 2; /* username/password */\n615:     /* write the number of authentication methods */\n616:     socksreq[1] = (unsigned char) (idx - 2);\n617: \n618:     sx->outp = socksreq;\n619:     sx->outstanding = idx;\n620:     presult = socks_state_send(cf, sx, data, CURLPX_SEND_CONNECT,\n621:                                \"initial SOCKS5 request\");\n622:     if(CURLPX_OK != presult)\n623:       return presult;\n624:     else if(sx->outstanding) {\n625:       /* remain in sending state */\n626:       return CURLPX_OK;\n627:     }\n628:     sxstate(sx, data, CONNECT_SOCKS_READ);\n629:     goto CONNECT_SOCKS_READ_INIT;\n630:   case CONNECT_SOCKS_SEND:\n631:     presult = socks_state_send(cf, sx, data, CURLPX_SEND_CONNECT,\n632:                                \"initial SOCKS5 request\");\n633:     if(CURLPX_OK != presult)\n634:       return presult;\n635:     else if(sx->outstanding) {\n636:       /* remain in sending state */\n637:       return CURLPX_OK;\n638:     }\n639:     /* FALLTHROUGH */\n640: CONNECT_SOCKS_READ_INIT:\n641:   case CONNECT_SOCKS_READ_INIT:\n642:     sx->outstanding = 2; /* expect two bytes */\n643:     sx->outp = socksreq; /* store it here */\n644:     /* FALLTHROUGH */\n645:   case CONNECT_SOCKS_READ:\n646:     presult = socks_state_recv(cf, sx, data, CURLPX_RECV_CONNECT,\n647:                                \"initial SOCKS5 response\");\n648:     if(CURLPX_OK != presult)\n649:       return presult;\n650:     else if(sx->outstanding) {\n651:       /* remain in reading state */\n652:       return CURLPX_OK;\n653:     }\n654:     else if(socksreq[0] != 5) {\n655:       failf(data, \"Received invalid version in initial SOCKS5 response.\");\n656:       return CURLPX_BAD_VERSION;\n657:     }\n658:     else if(socksreq[1] == 0) {\n659:       /* DONE! No authentication needed. Send request. */\n660:       sxstate(sx, data, CONNECT_REQ_INIT);\n661:       goto CONNECT_REQ_INIT;\n662:     }\n663:     else if(socksreq[1] == 2) {\n664:       /* regular name + password authentication */\n665:       sxstate(sx, data, CONNECT_AUTH_INIT);\n666:       goto CONNECT_AUTH_INIT;\n667:     }\n668: #if defined(HAVE_GSSAPI) || defined(USE_WINDOWS_SSPI)\n669:     else if(allow_gssapi && (socksreq[1] == 1)) {\n670:       sxstate(sx, data, CONNECT_GSSAPI_INIT);\n671:       result = Curl_SOCKS5_gssapi_negotiate(cf, data);\n672:       if(result) {\n673:         failf(data, \"Unable to negotiate SOCKS5 GSS-API context.\");\n674:         return CURLPX_GSSAPI;\n675:       }\n676:     }\n677: #endif\n678:     else {\n679:       /* error */\n680:       if(!allow_gssapi && (socksreq[1] == 1)) {\n681:         failf(data,\n682:               \"SOCKS5 GSSAPI per-message authentication is not supported.\");\n683:         return CURLPX_GSSAPI_PERMSG;\n684:       }\n685:       else if(socksreq[1] == 255) {\n686:         failf(data, \"No authentication method was acceptable.\");\n687:         return CURLPX_NO_AUTH;\n688:       }\n689:     }\n690:     failf(data,\n691:           \"Undocumented SOCKS5 mode attempted to be used by server.\");\n692:     return CURLPX_UNKNOWN_MODE;\n693: #if defined(HAVE_GSSAPI) || defined(USE_WINDOWS_SSPI)\n694:   case CONNECT_GSSAPI_INIT:\n695:     /* GSSAPI stuff done non-blocking */\n696:     break;\n697: #endif\n698: \n699:   default: /* do nothing! */\n700:     break;\n701: \n702: CONNECT_AUTH_INIT:\n703:   case CONNECT_AUTH_INIT: {\n704:     /* Needs user name and password */\n705:     size_t proxy_user_len, proxy_password_len;\n706:     if(sx->proxy_user && sx->proxy_password) {\n707:       proxy_user_len = strlen(sx->proxy_user);\n708:       proxy_password_len = strlen(sx->proxy_password);\n709:     }\n710:     else {\n711:       proxy_user_len = /* version (SOCKS4) */\\n312:     socksreq[1] = 1; /* connect */\\n313:     socksreq[2] = (unsigned char)((sx->remote_port >> 8) & 0xff); /* MSB */\\n314:     socksreq[3] = (unsigned char)(sx->remote_port & 0xff);   "content": "# Security Reachability Analysis: curl SOCKS5 Proxy Handler\n\n## 1. Summary\n\nThe `do_SOCKS5()` function in `lib/socks.c` implements the SOCKS5 proxy protocol handshake. This analysis traces the complete call path from curl's HTTP handler to the SOCKS5 proxy handler to determine if this function is reachable from external input.\n\n**Conclusion: REACHABLE from external input** (network data from SOCKS5 proxy server)\n\n---\n\n## 2. Affected Code\n\n**Function:** `do_SOCKS5()`\n**Location:** `lib/socks.c:548-1054`\n**Function Type:** Internal proxy handler (CURLproxycode)\n\n**Responsibility:**\nThe `do_SOCKS5()` function implements the complete SOCKS5 proxy negotiation state machine according to RFC 1928. It handles:\n- Initial SOCKS5 greeting and authentication method negotiation\n- Username/password authentication (SOCKS5 sub-negotiation)\n- GSS-API authentication (GSSAPI per-message security)\n- CONNECT request to establish a tunnel to the destination host\n- Parsing of SOCKS5 server responses with variable-length address fields\n\n---\n\n## 3. Attack Path: Complete Call Chain\n\n```\nUser Input (curl CLI or API)\n  \u2193\ncurl_easy_setopt(CURLOPT_PROXY, \"socks5://proxy:1080\")\n  \u2193\nCurl_http_connect() [lib/http.c:1565]\n  \u2502 Entry point for HTTP/HTTPS protocol handler\n  \u2193\nCurl_conn_connect() [lib/connect.c] (Connection filter setup)\n  \u2193\nMulti Interface: curl_multi_perform() \u2192 multi_runsingle()\n  \u2502 DNS Resolution: MSTATE_RESOLVING \u2192 MSTATE_RESOLVECOMPLETE [lib/multi.c:2001-2070]\n  \u2193\nCurl_once_resolved() [lib/hostip.c:1325]\n  \u2502 Called after DNS resolution completes\n  \u2193\nCurl_setup_conn() [lib/url.c:3858]\n  \u2502 Post-DNS connection setup\n  \u2193\nCurl_conn_setup() [lib/connect.c:1416]\n  \u2502 Creates connection filter chain\n  \u2193\ncf_setup_create() \u2192 cf_setup_connect() [lib/connect.c:1186]\n  \u2502 State machine for filter chain creation\n  \u2502 Checks: cf->conn->bits.socksproxy (set at lib/url.c:1547-1548)\n  \u2193\nCurl_cf_socks_proxy_insert_after() [lib/connect.c:1218]\n  \u2502 Inserts SOCKS proxy filter into chain\n  \u2193\nsocks_proxy_cf_connect() [lib/socks.c:1103]\n  \u2502 SOCKS proxy connection filter callback\n  \u2502 Initializes socks_state and sets:\n  \u2502 - sx->hostname: destination host\n  \u2502 - sx->remote_port: destination port\n  \u2502 - sx->proxy_user: proxy username (if configured)\n  \u2502 - sx->proxy_password: proxy password (if configured)\n  \u2193\nconnect_SOCKS() [lib/socks.c:1056]\n  \u2502 Switch statement routes to correct SOCKS version handler\n  \u2502 Condition: conn->socks_proxy.proxytype \u2208 {CURLPROXY_SOCKS5, CURLPROXY_SOCKS5_HOSTNAME}\n  \u2193\ndo_SOCKS5() [lib/socks.c:548] \u2190 VULNERABLE FUNCTION\n  \u2502 State machine with 18 states (enum connect_t)\n  \u2502 Receives and parses SOCKS5 server responses\n  \u2193\nNetwork Data Sources:\n  - SOCKS5 Proxy Server Response at proxy_addr:proxy_port\n  - Username/password echoed by proxy\n  - BND.ADDR and BND.PORT in response\n```\n\n### Key Functions in Call Chain\n\n| Function | Location | Role |\n|----------|----------|------|\n| `Curl_http_connect()` | lib/http.c:1565 | HTTP protocol handler entry point |\n| `Curl_conn_connect()` | lib/connect.c | Connection filter chain driver |\n| `curl_multi_perform()` | lib/multi.c | Multi-interface event loop |\n| `Curl_once_resolved()` | lib/hostip.c:1325 | Post-DNS setup trigger |\n| `Curl_setup_conn()` | lib/url.c:3858 | Connection filter chain initialization |\n| `cf_setup_connect()` | lib/connect.c:1186 | Filter chain state machine |\n| `Curl_cf_socks_proxy_insert_after()` | lib/connect.c:1218 | SOCKS filter insertion (conditional) |\n| `socks_proxy_cf_connect()` | lib/socks.c:1103 | SOCKS proxy filter callback |\n| `connect_SOCKS()` | lib/socks.c:1056 | SOCKS version dispatcher |\n| `do_SOCKS5()` | lib/socks.c:548 | **SOCKS5 protocol implementation** |\n\n---\n\n## 4. Severity Assessment\n\n### Reachability: YES - REACHABLE\n\n**Conditions Required:**\n1. **User Configuration (Mandatory):** The user MUST explicitly configure a SOCKS5 proxy via one of:\n   - Command-line: `curl --socks5 proxy.example.com:1080 https://target.com`\n   - Command-line: `curl --proxy socks5://proxy.example.com:1080 https://target.com`\n   - API: `curl_easy_setopt(curl, CURLOPT_PROXY, \"socks5://proxy.example.com:1080\")`\n   - Curl config: `socks5 = proxy.example.com:1080`\n\n2. **Network Connectivity (Mandatory):** A network connection to the proxy server must be established at `proxy_host:proxy_port`\n\n3. **Target URL (Mandatory):** User provides a target URL to connect through the proxy\n\n### Attack Vector\n\n**Primary:** Malicious SOCKS5 Proxy Server returning crafted responses\n\n**Secondary:** Network MITM attack on the path to the SOCKS5 proxy server (man-in-the-middle)\n\n### External Input Reaching do_SOCKS5()\n\nThe following network data from the SOCKS5 proxy server directly influences `do_SOCKS5()` behavior:\n\n1. **Initial Greeting Response (2 bytes minimum):**\n   - Byte 0: SOCKS version (0x05)\n   - Byte 1: Selected authentication method (0x00, 0x01, 0x02, 0xFF, etc.)\n\n2. **Authentication Sub-Negotiation Response (2 bytes minimum):**\n   - Byte 0: Sub-negotiation version\n   - Byte 1: Authentication status (0x00 = success)\n\n3. **CONNECT Request Response (10+ bytes):**\n   - Byte 0: SOCKS version (should be 0x05)\n   - Byte 1: Reply code (0x00 = success, 0x01-0x08 = various errors)\n   - Byte 2: Reserved (should be 0x00)\n   - Byte 3: ATYP - Address type (0x01=IPv4, 0x03=domain name, 0x04=IPv6)\n   - Bytes 4+: BND.ADDR (variable length, **UNTRUSTED from proxy**)\n   - Bytes N+(4-6): BND.PORT (2 bytes, **UNTRUSTED from proxy**)\n\n### Data Flow Analysis\n\n```\nNetwork (Proxy Server)\n    \u2193\n    \u251c\u2500\u2192 socksreq[0-1]: Initial response\n    \u251c\u2500\u2192 socksreq[0-1]: Auth response\n    \u2514\u2500\u2192 socksreq[0-9+]: CONNECT response\n         \u2193\n    Parsed in do_SOCKS5():\n    - Line 654: Check socksreq[0] == 0x05 (version)\n    - Line 658: Check socksreq[1] for auth method\n    - Line 960-985: Parse CONNECT response error codes\n    - Line 1005-1020: Calculate packet size from socksreq[3-4]\n         \u2193\n    Vulnerability Analysis (see below)\n```\n\n---\n\n## 5. Remediation & Security Analysis\n\n### Buffer Overflow Analysis\n\n**Critical Code Section:** `lib/socks.c:1004-1030`\n\n```c\n1004:     /* Calculate real packet size */\n1005:     if(socksreq[3] == 3) {\n1006:       /* domain name */\n1007:       int addrlen = (int) socksreq[4];\n1008:       len = 5 + addrlen + 2;\n1009:     }\n```\n\n**Potential Issue:** Domain name length field (`socksreq[4]`) is read directly from untrusted proxy response.\n\n**Safety Assessment:**\n- `socksreq[4]` is a single byte (max value 255)\n- Calculation: `len = 5 + addrlen + 2` \u2192 maximum value = 5 + 255 + 2 = 262 bytes\n- Buffer size: `READBUFFER_MIN = 1024` bytes (defined in lib/urldata.h:203)\n- **Conclusion: NO buffer overflow** (262 << 1024)\n\n### Hostname Length Truncation Analysis\n\n**Critical Code Section:** `lib/socks.c:589-592, 906`\n\n```c\n589:     if(!socks5_resolve_local && hostname_len > 255) {\n590:       infof(data, \"SOCKS5: server resolving disabled for hostnames of \"\n591:             \"length > 255 [actual len=%zu]\", hostname_len);\n592:       socks5_resolve_local = TRUE;\n593:     }\n...\n906:     socksreq[len++] = (char) hostname_len; /* one byte address length */\n```\n\n**Potential Issue:** If `hostname_len > 255`, casting to `(char)` truncates the value.\n\n**Safety Assessment:**\n- Bounds check at line 589 forces local resolution if `hostname_len > 255`\n- State machine ensures remote resolution path only taken when `!socks5_resolve_local`\n- Logic prevents remote resolution with long hostnames\n- **Conclusion: NO truncation vulnerability** (protected by bounds check)\n\n### Input Validation Summary\n\n| Input Field | Source | Validation | Risk Level |\n|-------------|--------|-----------|-----------|\n| SOCKS version byte | Network | `socksreq[0] == 5` check at line 654, 960 | Low |\n| Auth method byte | Network | Array bounds check (values 0-255 valid) | Low |\n| Auth response | Network | Status byte checked at line 772 | Low |\n| ATYP byte | Network | Switch statement validates 1, 3, 4 (line 1005-1020) | Low |\n| Domain length byte | Network | Max 255, buffer 1024 bytes, no overflow | Low |\n| IPv4 address | Network | Fixed 4 bytes | Low |\n| IPv6 address | Network | Fixed 16 bytes | Low |\n| Port number | Network | Fixed 2 bytes | Low |\n\n### Existing Protections\n\n1. **Buffer bounds:** READBUFFER_MIN (1024 bytes) enforced at compile time\n2. **Hostname length:** Pre-checks at line 589 prevent truncation\n3. **Protocol validation:** ATYP field validated (line 1017-1019)\n4. **Version checks:** SOCKS version must be 0x05 (line 654, 960)\n5. **State machine:** Prevents out-of-order operations via enum connect_t\n\n---\n\n## 6. Conclusion\n\n### Reachability Status\n\n\u2705 **REACHABLE from external input**\n\nThe `do_SOCKS5()` function IS reachable from network input when:\n1. A SOCKS5 proxy is explicitly configured by the user\n2. The proxy server responds with crafted data\n\n### Security Posture\n\n\u2705 **APPEARS SECURE** with current implementation\n\n**Key Findings:**\n- No obvious buffer overflow vulnerabilities in response parsing\n- Proper bounds checking prevents hostname length issues\n- Network data parsing uses defensive programming (explicit length checks)\n- State machine prevents protocol violations\n\n**Recommendation:**\n- Continue validating all network-sourced fields before use\n- Maintain strict bounds checks on variable-length fields\n- Regular fuzzing against malformed SOCKS5 responses recommended\n\n### Attack Prerequisites\n\nAn attacker could exploit this code only if:\n1. User voluntarily configures a SOCKS5 proxy (user-controlled)\n2. Attacker controls the SOCKS5 proxy server OR performs MITM attack\n3. Attacker sends carefully crafted SOCKS5 responses\n\n**Risk Assessment:** MEDIUM (requires user configuration + network control)\n\n---\n\n## 7. Sources Analyzed\n\n- `lib/socks.c`: SOCKS4/SOCKS5 proxy handler (1254 lines)\n- `lib/socks.h`: SOCKS proxy header\n- `lib/connect.c`: Connection filter chain management\n- `lib/http.c`: HTTP protocol handler\n- `lib/hostip.c`: DNS resolution interface\n- `lib/url.c`: Connection initialization\n- `lib/multi.c`: Multi-interface state machine\n- `lib/urldata.h`: Data structures and constants\n",

/* one byte address length */\n```\n\n**Potential Issue:** If `hostname_len > 255`, casting to `(char)` truncates the value.\n\n**Safety Assessment:**\n- Bounds check at line 589 forces local resolution if `hostname_len > 255`\n- State machine ensures remote resolution path only taken when `!socks5_resolve_local`\n- Logic prevents remote resolution with long hostnames\n- **Conclusion: NO truncation vulnerability** (protected by bounds check)\n\n### Input Validation Summary\n\n| Input Field | Source | Validation | Risk Level |\n|-------------|--------|-----------|-----------|\n| SOCKS version byte | Network | `socksreq[0] == 5` check at line 654, 960 | Low |\n| Auth method byte | Network | Array bounds check (values 0-255 valid) | Low |\n| Auth response | Network | Status byte checked at line 772 | Low |\n| ATYP byte | Network | Switch statement validates 1, 3, 4 (line 1005-1020) | Low |\n| Domain length byte | Network | Max 255, buffer 1024 bytes, no overflow | Low |\n| IPv4 address | Network | Fixed 4 bytes | Low |\n| IPv6 address | Network | Fixed 16 bytes | Low |\n| Port number | Network | Fixed 2 bytes | Low |\n\n### Existing Protections\n\n1. **Buffer bounds:** READBUFFER_MIN (1024 bytes) enforced at compile time\n2. **Hostname length:** Pre-checks at line 589 prevent truncation\n3. **Protocol validation:** ATYP field validated (line 1017-1019)\n4. **Version checks:** SOCKS version must be 0x05 (line 654, 960)\n5. **State machine:** Prevents out-of-order operations via enum connect_t\n\n---\n\n## 6. Conclusion\n\n### Reachability Status\n\n\u2705 **REACHABLE from external input**\n\nThe `do_SOCKS5()` function IS reachable from network input when:\n1. A SOCKS5 proxy is explicitly configured by the user\n2. The proxy server responds with crafted data\n\n### Security Posture\n\n\u2705 **APPEARS SECURE** with current implementation\n\n**Key Findings:**\n- No obvious buffer overflow vulnerabilities in response parsing\n- Proper bounds checking prevents hostname length issues\n- Network data parsing uses defensive programming (explicit length checks)\n- State machine prevents protocol violations\n\n**Recommendation:**\n- Continue validating all network-sourced fields before use\n- Maintain strict bounds checks on variable-length fields\n- Regular fuzzing against malformed SOCKS5 responses recommended\n\n### Attack Prerequisites\n\nAn attacker could exploit this code only if:\n1. User voluntarily configures a SOCKS5 proxy (user-controlled)\n2. Attacker controls the SOCKS5 proxy server OR performs MITM attack\n3. Attacker sends carefully crafted SOCKS5 responses\n\n**Risk Assessment:** MEDIUM (requires user configuration + network control)\n\n---\n\n## 7. # Security Reachability Analysis: curl SOCKS5 Proxy Handler

## 1. Summary

The `do_SOCKS5()` function in `lib/socks.c` implements the SOCKS5 proxy protocol handshake. This analysis traces the complete call path from curl's HTTP handler to the SOCKS5 proxy handler to determine if this function is reachable from external input.

**Conclusion: REACHABLE from external input** (network data from SOCKS5 proxy server)

---

## 2. Affected Code

**Function:** `do_SOCKS5()`
**Location:** `lib/socks.c:548-1054`
**Function Type:** Internal proxy handler (CURLproxycode)

**Responsibility:**
The `do_SOCKS5()` function implements the complete SOCKS5 proxy negotiation state machine according to RFC 1928. It handles:
- Initial SOCKS5 greeting and authentication method negotiation
- Username/password authentication (SOCKS5 sub-negotiation)
- GSS-API authentication (GSSAPI per-message security)
- CONNECT request to establish a tunnel to the destination host
- Parsing of SOCKS5 server responses with variable-length address fields

---

## 3. Attack Path: Complete Call Chain

```
User Input (curl CLI or API)
  ↓
curl_easy_setopt(CURLOPT_PROXY, "socks5://proxy:1080")
  ↓
Curl_http_connect() [lib/http.c:1565]
  │ Entry point for HTTP/HTTPS protocol handler
  ↓
Curl_conn_connect() [lib/connect.c] (Connection filter setup)
  ↓
Multi Interface: curl_multi_perform() → multi_runsingle()
  │ DNS Resolution: MSTATE_RESOLVING → MSTATE_RESOLVECOMPLETE [lib/multi.c:2001-2070]
  ↓
Curl_once_resolved() [lib/hostip.c:1325]
  │ Called after DNS resolution completes
  ↓
Curl_setup_conn() [lib/url.c:3858]
  │ Post-DNS connection setup
  ↓
Curl_conn_setup() [lib/connect.c:1416]
  │ Creates connection filter chain
  ↓
cf_setup_create() → cf_setup_connect() [lib/connect.c:1186]
  │ State machine for filter ch
... (truncated)
